< review>
I found out about the place because of Netflix documentary Chef's Table and since then always wanted to go and meet Chef Takao and taste his food. I finally got to go and ordered the Omakase menu. It was a whole new and different experience and I got to taste really different Japanese dishes from what I'm used to in my country and my trips abroad. It was quite an interesting experience overall and I even got to take a picture with Takao! He's a very nice and humble person. Service is very good, starting from the moment you book your reservation. The restaurant has kind of a family vibe and they make you feel very welcomed. That's probably why a lot of locals visit the place and are regular customers. I stayed for a while talking to one of those customers and got the chance to speak a little bit with Takao and his crew. It's definitely a place you want to visit if you have the chance. Enjoy!< /review>

<Review>We ate lite so didn't venture far into the menu; that didn't keep us from admiring the BEAUTIFUL things distributed to fellow diners over the night or overhearing pleased diners who enthused openly (sometimes loudly) over something delicious. When I entered most of the tables had reserved signs. They were filled from that point on in the evening.

The sushi we did get was quiet and delicious. Texture is sometimes the most important thing in raw foods. You don't notice it so much unless it's bad, or really good. It's really good at Takao. Their little rolls looked beautiful. Things resting on banana leaves, cooked items, looked delicious.

The decor is clean, simple and light. It's much more lovely than it appears from outside. It's a little tight, especially at the sushi bar where we sat.

Overall, very nice.<//Review></record></dataset><record>

< text>
Very well kept up, attractive place, smooth floors for rolling carts. No peeling paint or anything like that.

Secure: Requires individual codes to get into elevator or through doors.

Clean: Other places I've stored in not al. In other places my clothes had evidence of mice nesting in em, had to throw a lot out. Not here. Never a single sign of any insects or mice. Yay!!!

In some other places I would open my unit a few months later and find a layer of dirt, dust, grit all over, had to wet-wipe everything. That was aggravating, having all my possessions dirty.

This place, however, is the cleanest of any storage place I've found.

Hours til 7pm so you can get by after work.

Only slight drawback is parking turnaround can be a little tight if you have a long truck...but it's doable.

Staff: Keisha is the woman at the front desk who usually helps me, and she is a total gem.

She's efficient and pro (handles renting or changing units smoothly and quickly) but also gives her work that personal touch missing so many places.

Unlike so many businesses where you're just an acct #, she remembers your name, is always cheerful, never in a bad mood, makes renting here a joy.

Heck, thinking about it, one reason I probably come back to deal with my storage and stay here is her. It's a pleasant experience all around. (But I'm sure that's true for many others too.)

Go here when you need to store stuff!< /text>

<Rating>4<//Rating>< review>
A big thank-you to employee Jim Nesbit for providing customer service above and beyond the call of duty. I stopped by a few minutes before closing time to ask a few questions since I was beginning the process of looking for a storage space to rent in San Francisco. Despite the fact that the facility was about to close for the night, Jim took the time to answer my questions and to provide all the information I would need to know as a prospective renter. Without having any certainty yet as to whether or not I was prepared to follow through and make a decision at that time, Jim nonetheless even made the extra effort to escort me to the third floor and actually show me the particular storage unit that I had under consideration. Because it was the only one currently available in the size and price range most appropriate to my needs, I decided then  and there to go ahead and rent the unit lest someone else do so and I miss out. At no time did I ever feel rushed or pressured by Jim in any way, and this is something I appreciate whenever doing business with anyone. The facility itself physically appears to be very clean and well-maintained. My only complaint concerns the company's main ad that comes up online promising free rent for the first month in San Francisco. Upon further inquiry, I learned that special offers such as this are apparently only made available in actual fact for a very small number of specific rental units. Therefore, in my opinion, the ad is somewhat misleading because it makes a promise without stating any restrictions or qualifications that would preclude the offer being generally applicable to all of the units currently for rent.</review>

<user_id>103945327243472831182<//user_id><name>Rebecca Huddleston</name>< Date>
1509638195555</Date>
< rate>
1</rate>
< review>
Im not sure how a place where both needle addicts and the genuinely homeless are living in droves inside the storage units gets anything above 1 star.

My boyfriend and I are native SFers so it should probably come as no surprise that our city and police either dont know or care about the state this place.

This business appeared innocuous on our quick tour but we have since realized the reality. We have to bring mase and our dog when we visit and we never visit alone. Doors are always propped open. The addict population knows the gate code and enters and exists at their leisure via the back ally (Stevenson).

Clearly after a few months here we are ending our contract.

While we of course empathise with the truly homeless living here  (we see them getting up and dressing for work and interviews and we often say hello) the number of needle addicts and mentally ill is shocking. Their living conditions are shocking. They live in storage units among nests of torn newspaper and piles of collected things. On our floor alone there are probably 20 people living. Perhaps ours is the only floor, dont know as we are afraid to "explore".

We are torn about reporting this place. On the one hand some of these folks trying to work or find work will be out of a roof over their heads. On the other hand, our encounters with those who are using or memtally unstable have been downright scary- and their living conditions are not great.

Please not support this front and these unsafe living conditions and unsafe renter conditions by storing here. There are several other well run choices in Mission Dolores listed on google and yelp.<//review>
